Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Natural Science Lecture

The Crisis of Natural Science

— Sijing

The world today is full of crises. There are political crises, economic crises, and strangely enough, even natural science, which serves as the model for science (including natural science and social science), is in crisis!

I think that most people who have not studied deeply will be surprised: Isn't this the era of natural science's omnipotence for the past few hundred years? The progress of human society in the past three hundred years surpasses that of the previous thousands of years; the improvement of material life, the development of productivity, and the rapid progress of civilization—are these not all gifts of natural science? Moreover, as society progresses, inventions and discoveries continue to emerge endlessly. From this perspective, natural science is not only the mother of civilization, but its future also seems very prosperous, and it is certainly not in crisis.

But if you look at it from another perspective, it will surprise you again: No matter how much natural science progresses, we have seen with our own eyes many people who are themselves great scientists, and who have even made inventions and discoveries in science, doubt science itself. They believe that science is not the "ultimate knowledge," and cannot thoroughly study the "true meaning" of the universe, and that science itself will reach a dead end, discovering its own falsehood and destruction. Therefore, science is unreliable and one must seek refuge in God and religion. For example, Heisenberg, Eddington, Jeans and other modern great scientists have said this. They have proved from scientific research that the objective universe is illusory, and only subjective existence is real. The development of wave mechanics has led to the establishment of the "uncertainty principle," thereby denying the law of causality and necessity in the objective world; the development of electrical science has led to the establishment of the theory that "matter has been destroyed"; the progress of mechanical research has led to the "separation of matter and energy theory," "independent existence of energy theory," and other theories. Other examples, such as the establishment of the theory of relativity, say that time and space only exist in the observer's subjectivity. All of these indicate that the theories of natural science are proving that the universe is unreal.

The reason why natural science reached the stage of science earlier than other sciences is that its research object is the objective, tangible material world, unlike social science or thought science, whose research objects are more unpredictable and difficult to grasp and analyze. Moreover, the methods of natural science are also empirical, such as the inductive method and the experimental method. In short, natural science was originally materialistic, so it was easy to become a science. But why is it now not working, unable to progress, and has to retreat into the quagmire of metaphysics to seek refuge in God and religion? Is this really a crisis of natural science itself?

Obviously, the evils that mankind has created or is in the process of creating—war, with its ferocity and cruelty—are entirely aided by science. Therefore, many humanitarian people who are concerned about the world believe that this is the fault of science itself. But in reality, science is beneficial to mankind. As for its assistance in the slaughter of mankind, this is not the sin of science itself, but the sin of a few people in society who use science to seek their own interests and destroy others, thereby also destroying mankind. Similarly, the crisis of natural science is not something that is bound to happen and cannot be avoided, but is due to the fact that natural scientists are limited by their social class, and cannot grasp the ever-progressing natural science. Because of their distorted worldview, because of their mechanical and outdated methodology, they not only cannot promote the development of science, but also hinder it.

Natural science, like art and literature, is part of the superstructure of society. Moreover, natural science has a more direct relationship with productivity than other ideologies, and it is easier to promote productivity and have a reciprocal effect on it. Because of this, when the productivity of the infrastructure is constrained and cannot develop, the natural science that is directly related to it will also be stagnant or in crisis. The current economic panic and political crisis are entirely due to the fact that the production relations of the social system hinder the development of productivity, and indirectly also hinder the development of natural science. For example, productivity could originally continue to develop, but in this capitalist society, where the purpose is to make profits, most hardworking people who do not have the means of production and only sell their labor do not have the money to buy the large quantities of goods produced by very advanced machinery, and therefore a panic of overproduction occurs. In this panic, production stagnates, and therefore natural science, which promotes the technological progress of production, is also forced to stagnate. Because if science progresses further, technology will be more developed, production will increase more, and at the same time, production will be more surplus and more panicked, so it has to be stopped. This is the crisis of the social system reflected in the crisis of natural science, but this is by no means a crisis of natural science itself.

Next, let's see what the characteristics of the current crisis of natural science are. In the last decade of the nineteenth century, the discovery of X-rays, radium, and radioactive rays caused enormous changes in physics. The two principles of "conservation of mass" and "conservation of energy" seemed to have been overturned. In the twentieth century, the discovery of the principle of relativity added another layer of chaos. It seems that as long as we discuss the equality of mass and energy according to the theory of relativity, the most important energy will disappear and escape. So, what caused such an absurd conclusion? This is not the reason for natural science itself. In reality, it is because the initial natural science, its research objects were still very simple, the research on each object was not very deep, and the scope of research was not very broad, so the principles of mechanism and the empirical method were enough to use. But when new inventions increase and reach deeper and larger fields, the previous partial, outdated, and mechanical viewpoints and methods can no longer control this vast material. So, as a result, it cannot analyze the materials it has excavated with existing methods, so it is suspicious and says "matter has been destroyed!" "Energy exists independently!" In short, this is due to idealism and the mechanical formal logic. This is also because the entire infrastructure is being prevented from moving forward, and it is reflected in ideology, and it becomes subjectivism, mechanism, etc. As for the mechanical materialism viewpoint of the early stage of natural science, it still poisons it and constitutes a part of its crisis.

So, how can the crisis of natural science be overcome? This must also be said from two aspects: The crisis from the social aspect is the main crisis. This cannot be escaped simply from natural science itself. It is necessary to make productivity unfettered and able to move forward freely. Therefore, the current production relations that bind the development of productivity—that is, the social system—must be changed, and natural science can then develop. This is not only a problem of natural science, but also a problem of social science and social reform. Finally, we must input new viewpoints and new methods into the research of natural science, and use more inclusive and comprehensive correct new viewpoints to study natural science. For example, if we stand on the position of materialism, the conclusion that "matter has been destroyed" will not be reached, because regardless of whether you are electricity, energy, mass, or quantity, it is nothing more than a form of existence of matter, but one of its attributes. These forms of existence and attributes, no matter how they change, are always independent of our subject. Also, if we use dynamic logic, we will not advocate "separation of matter and energy theory" or "independent energy theory," but advocate "unity of matter and energy theory," because all matter exists in motion and change, and all matter can also be transformed into each other at the same time. If we use the above viewpoints and methods, the so-called "uncertainty principle," the problem of biological mutations, etc., can be properly resolved. Also, we must follow the development of natural science to predict its future laws, and should not stubbornly stick to the established realm and completely use the past to measure the present and the future. Because in the process of progress, the research itself can develop its methods. For example, the advocacy of the uncertainty principle is due to the study of the movement of electrons in atoms, but what is the structure of the space inside the atom is not yet known. We should actively work to study the structure of the extremely small space inside the atom, and the theory of the uncertainty principle will be self-defeating in the future. Therefore, in continuous research, some mistakes are also made, but at the same time, some mistakes will be overcome. Combining the above methods, the crisis of natural science may be eliminated?

Essays

The Great Fire on the Banks of the Luan River

— Yu Zhang

It was three o'clock in the afternoon. Having a few hours of free time, I went for a walk outside the school, slowly walking along the Luan River embankment east of the city. About an hour later, I turned back towards the school and met my good friend Zhiqing.

"Shunan! Hurry! What books do you have? Quickly check them! Destroy anything that 'they' deem inappropriate!" Zhiqing said to me with both sorrow and anxiety.

"What's going on?" I was bewildered, not knowing why he was so anxious.

"This... it's not convenient to talk here. Come to the study hall—you'll understand." He shook his head, grabbed my hand, and dragged me to the study hall. The road to the study hall was very quiet; I didn't see a single classmate—only a few school servants hurrying back and forth in a state of panic. "What happened?" I kept wondering as I approached the study hall door.

In the study hall, there were many classmates. Some looked very disheveled, some even had tears in their eyes as if they were about to cry, and some were muttering to themselves, not knowing what they were saying. These classmates were all gritting their teeth, checking their own bookshelves and cabinets. Clearly, some disaster had occurred! The smell of burnt paper entered my nostrils, evoking the unpleasant feeling of burning paper money after someone's death. In the middle of the room, a pile of flames stretched very high, almost licking the ceiling. Students were still continuously throwing their books, scraps of paper, and letters into the fire, and sadness and resentment filled everyone's heart! At this moment, I truly felt like I was lost in a fog. My nerves were confused, and I just stood there staring at them.

Page 22

My heart kept asking, "Why are they burning books in the study hall?" But my mouth couldn't say it! My classmates also occasionally turned their heads to glance at me, as if they didn't recognize me. After burning their books, the classmates hurriedly left, wanting to find a safe haven, but this land was still in "their" hands! After a while, I heard the sound of hurried footsteps outside the room.

I immediately woke up from my dream and quickly asked Zhiqing to tell me what had happened.

"Just now, our principal was surrounded by the constabulary of the Eastern Hebei Government. They came to inquire about the 'Teachers' Union' distributing leaflets at the Ao Dong Games; at the same time, the military department called saying they were coming to inspect the school…" Zhiqing hadn't finished speaking when his face had already turned pale. His voice stimulated his heart, and he couldn't continue speaking.

Yu Zhou, another classmate burning books in the stove room, heard the footsteps in the study hall and hurriedly opened the door to look around.

"Yu Zhou!" This was the anxious voice of the Dean of Students; "Don't burn them in the study hall—who will be responsible if the building catches fire? And isn't the ash on the ground just giving 'them' more suspicion? Or… they're about to come—…"

"Oh dear!" I heard myself exclaim. I felt as if I had been thrown into cold ice. I suddenly remembered the "Educational New Tide" I bought… here it comes. These were all considered forbidden by "them" and written on the police station's announcements.

"This is too dangerous!" I thought; and immediately went to open my book cabinet, dragging out all the magazines, letters from a certain newspaper office, envelopes, "Educational New Tide," and my own manuscripts. I carefully checked everything repeatedly, and then asked Zhiqing to help me destroy them together. "Come on, let's go burn them at the public stove." Saying that, I dragged Zhiqing away.

The area in front of the public stove was already crowded with classmates, and there was no room for us to squeeze in. Two classmates were arguing with each other because one of them wanted to squeeze forward. My heart was filled with panic, "When will I be able to finish? The inspectors might be coming!" I thought.

The water in the tea kettle was boiling hot. The small room was filled with steam, and you could hardly see the person across from you. The students' hearts and mouths were weighed down by a heavy stone of sorrow. There wasn't a sound in the room, only the sound of paper burning and the sighs from the water kettle breaking the deathly silence. The fire was extremely large, and paper ashes poured out from the chimney continuously.

I couldn't wait any longer. I went to squat at the corner of the wall outside the public stove house and started burning my books—my beloved books—on the mud ground! I was very afraid that the fire would spread like wildfire… my hands were trembling… my heart was pounding… my body was getting hot… Alas! Students of Luandong!

World Knowledge

The Lone Island in the North Sea That Will Sink

— Wu Hua

According to geographers, the sea from the Scandinavian Peninsula to Holland and Germany was entirely a solid ice sea in ancient times. Around 25,000 years ago, due to climate conditions, the ice sea melted and became the North Sea as it is today. In the North Sea, there is a lone island struggling against the sea waves, with an area of less than 250 acres, which is the unfortunate Helgoland Island.

According to scientists' estimates, the unfortunate island of Helgoland was originally five times larger than it is now when it first appeared. However, because it has been constantly attacked by raging waves and eroded by the sea since its emergence, its territory has been shrinking day by day. In the past hundred years alone, it has been losing about one acre of area every ten years. At this rate, its existence is certainly a cause for concern.

However, the erosion of the sea waves on this lone island is very chronic and not like the imperialist aggression against weak nations, which quickly swallows it all up. Judging from the current situation, the island's lifespan is at least three to four thousand years. Therefore, the two thousand islanders currently living on the island do not find the continued erosion of the entire island by sea waves frightening. What they are most worried about is the fate of a mile-long sandbar in the eastern sea of the island. Because this sandbar can be said to be the lifeline of the entire island; if it sinks, the lives of the islanders on the lone island will immediately be in dire straits. Why is this sandbar so important to them? This is hard to explain in a few words.

Originally, in the northwest of the sandbar, between the island and the sandbar, there is a white cliff, as the islanders call it. There, high-quality chalk (white earth) is extracted, first by Hamburg merchants! At the same time, the islanders rely on doing this work for a living. Unfortunately, due to the attacks of storms and raging waves, the large white cliff, which stood 200 feet above the water, was destroyed. Now, only the shadow of the cliff top can be seen at low tide, becoming a large reef. This cannot but be said to be nature's playfulness with mankind.

After losing the white cliff, the only way for the islanders of the lone island to survive is to catch fish and seabirds. In 1806, Napoleon captured Berlin and actively sought to conquer Europe; in order to conquer Britain, he imposed an economic blockade on it, prohibiting European countries from trading with it and forbidding British and its colonial ships from stopping at European ports. As a result, the British were forced to pay attention to the lone island of Helgoland and saw it as an excellent place for secret trade. For a time, British stores rushed to establish branches in Shanghai, and merchants often came here to engage in business, giving this unfortunate North Sea island the elegant name of "Little London" and making it a considerable commercial city; and the lives of the island's residents were thus somewhat improved. But later, this fortunate economic blockade against Britain was lifted, and secret trade was naturally no longer necessary. Helgoland Island became British territory, so the islanders lost their source of income again and suffered a tragic fate.

It is truly necessary to thank God. When the islanders of the lone island fell back into a state of poverty, one of their experts suddenly had a flash of inspiration and came up with a plan, which was to plan to open a seawater bathing beach on the sandbar to attract visitors from Northern European countries to come here to escape the summer heat. This plan succeeded after a long period of effort and overcoming many difficulties. Now, during the three or four months of summer each year, there are thousands of people from Germany and Northern European countries who come here to escape the summer heat and bathe. The spending of these visitors in three or four months is the source of livelihood for the islanders of the lone island.

However, now this sandbar only appears a few feet above the water at high tide; in the event of an extraordinary storm attack, a huge wave attack, it is in danger of being completely destroyed. This is simply an unimaginable thing for the islanders of the lone island.

Now, Helgoland Island belongs to Germany. The process by which the Germans obtained the island and what they have done here is not very simple. As mentioned above, this lone island was originally occupied by the British. It was only in 1890 that the British transferred it to the Germans. In order to obtain this North Sea island that will sink, Germany gave some of its colonies in East Friesland to the British. This is undoubtedly very thought-provoking. Germany's willingness to acquire this lone island at a significant cost certainly has its great intentions. Because in Germany's view, although this is a small lone island, it also has great military value. After obtaining the island, it immediately began to build a large military port here. On the one hand, it set up artillery positions in the commanding heights of the highlands and placed artillery pieces; on the other hand, it built tunnels between the military port and the artillery positions to store food, making it a major naval base for Germany. The Germans have also worked hard to defend against the attacks of wind and waves through artificial means, especially in the western part where the waves attack most fiercely, and have built large projects, as a result, the shrinking of the island has been greatly reduced. However, since the island itself is not composed of solid rock strata, it is difficult to resist the attacks of wind, rain, and waves.

After the outbreak of World War I in 1914, Germany immediately forced the islanders to take their necessary belongings and board refugee ships to Hamburg within a few hours, and their remaining property was of course unconditionally occupied by the German army. During the four years and four months of the Great War, the islanders were used as cannon fodder by Germany, and many of them died; only a small number of survivors returned to this unfortunate island after the war to rely on the beach of the sandbar and live their unfortunate lives.

After the war, according to the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, all military facilities on the island were dismantled. It is a bit terrifying to say that it took almost three years to dismantle the artillery positions and military port facilities, and every day there were explosions with rumbling sounds, and long-term earthquakes shook this North Sea island and the unfortunate people on it.

Now, the situation in Europe is more urgent than in 1914. Hitler has torn up the Treaty of Versailles, and his ambitious eyes can turn to Northern Europe at any time, so this North Sea island is likely to be re-armed at any time.

Confessions of a Working Woman

Female Factory Workers

— Ms. Chen Ying Talks

Every morning, the sky is just barely getting light, right? But for us who are used to hearing it, we have long heard the buzzing first echo from the factory chimney. At this time, the people who enjoy life are probably still in their dreams! But we have to quickly get out of bed and quickly wash up. Often before you can wash up leisurely, the buzzing second echo seems to be cursing us, calling us to hurry up! Hurry up! We have to quickly leave home and rush quickly to the factory. Because the third echo follows, and the factory's iron gate will be closed right after. However, I don't think I've ever seen the factory's black gate closed, which shows that I've never been late once. Although there have been several times when it was very dangerous, that is, when I felt like I was getting sick, my head was splitting, and I was too tired to get up, but when I thought about having to pay the bills and eat, I immediately felt like someone had poured a basin of cold water on my head, making it easy for me to get up and go out the door!

Generally speaking, we can earn about thirteen or fourteen yuan per month per person. However, this refers to skilled workers who have been working for one or two years. They are all paid by piecework, and how much they earn each day is calculated according to the prescribed price per piece. If it is a novice, it is different. At first hearing, it will make those who want to become female workers frown. According to the rules of our ×× yarn factory, any new person who comes in does not get any money at all in the first month. Only after learning will they get two jiao and five fen per day; the first time they get paid monthly, they can only take twenty days of wages. Ten days are counted as stored work, and the money for this stored work can only be returned to you or given to your family when you stop working or die.

Speaking of this income, it is naturally not enough to cover expenses. However, if parents, sisters, and brothers can all work in the factory, then, if everyone's income is combined and used by everyone, it will be quite ample. If it is a single person, it costs about ten yuan per month to live in a house and eat, and sometimes they have to send some money to their parents living in the countryside, or have small social engagements, so they always feel that their money is not enough. Fortunately, their lives are quite careful and frugal. For example, when renting a house, most of them rent a kitchen shed together with two or three people. A slightly better one is the back building, but most of them rent the attic; eating is also cooked by everyone together. Because only in this way can everyone spare some time to do some odd jobs around the house. For example, if she cooks today, I can take the opportunity to wash my clothes; if I cook tomorrow, she can do her odd jobs. You know we are very busy. We enter the factory every day from five forty-five in the morning and have to work until six o'clock in the evening before we can go home. There is only one hour of rest in the middle for eating. We bring our own lunch in lunch baskets. Most of us cook rice and vegetables and bring some dried radish, watermelon rind, and other pickles to eat.

The yarn factory is densely packed with textile machines taller than people. Floss is constantly spewing out from those dog-tooth-like "spindles," flying everywhere like snowflakes and willow catkins. The room is full of it, and you can choke to death if you're not careful. But after a long time, you get used to it.

Even so, the people in our factory are the happiest among the female workers. Our factory is not small in scope. It weaves 1,400 bolts of ten-pound cloth and produces 40,000 flour sacks every day. As far as I know, the number of male and female workers in the whole factory is 2,100 just for those who live in the factory. The factory's employee dormitory is divided into four areas. The first area is the female worker trainee (novice) dormitory, with 50 bedrooms, each housing ten or more people, currently housing a total of 524 people. The second area is the single female worker (skilled worker) dormitory, with a total of 30 buildings, each with two floors, currently housing 611 people, also with ten or more people living in each room. The third area is specially for workers with families to live in, with a total of 33 buildings, currently housing 594 people. The fourth area is the single male worker dormitory, with 33 bedrooms, currently housing 401 people. Areas one and four are long rows of Western-style buildings with three floors, completely built of cement and steel. Hot and cold running water, iron beds, dining halls, sanitary toilets, bathrooms, washrooms, reading rooms, classrooms, and other facilities are very complete. There are also regulations: All female workers living in areas one, two, and three must go to area one to bathe once a day: male workers living in areas three and four must go to area four to bathe once a day. As for the facilities in areas two and three, they are only like ordinary alley houses outside the factory, but the prices are extremely cheap, and the expenses can be saved more than outside. The factory also has a consumer cooperative located near the center of each area, selling all daily necessities, including yarn, cloth, firewood, rice, oil, salt, sauce, vinegar, tea, sugar, and other items. In terms of public health, there is also a five-story employee hospital, employing a medical director and a female obstetrics director, as well as two female nurses and a Chinese medicine doctor. All factory employees can receive free diagnosis and treatment. In addition, there is also a club, where there is a reading room, a library, a billiards room, and under the guidance of staff members, workers have organized basketball teams, tennis teams, football teams, ping-pong teams, opera troupes, drama troupes, music bands, and martial arts classes, etc., and all employees can freely participate in activities at the prescribed times. Moreover, we also have to receive compulsory education! It is said that there are several tutoring schools in our factory: divided into morning and evening schools for male workers, and morning and evening schools for female workers. All factory employees must serve as volunteer teachers in this school.

However, in some places, the facilities seem to be incomplete, so that workers are often injured and have their limbs broken by the machine belts. In Yangshupu, you can often hear a very miserable "wuwuwu" sound. That means that among our group of laborers, another one has suffered misfortune!

Fable

Fresh Water

— Chen Ruhui

The passenger ship "Adel" sailed out of the Hettara Strait, carrying a full load of passengers. The sharp-angled bow pierced the sea surface, breaking through the surging waves and spraying white foam; the tall chimney carried a long, thick black smoke trail, stretching far across the endless water. This monster-like large ship proceeded steadily forward amid the rising and falling of the sea and the shining of the sunlight. The shipowner happily smoked a cigar and paced lightly back and forth on the deck.

The passenger ship sailed day and night. The machinery in the engine room rattled incessantly, and the chimney continued to spew out black smoke. Everything was beautiful, and everything was filled with an atmosphere of peace, but the shipowner's brow was furrowed; he no longer strolled leisurely, nor did he happily smoke his cigar. He went into the kitchen and then went out again; this strange behavior attracted the attention of the passengers, so they asked the shipowner to announce the mystery, and surrounded him, firmly demanding that he explain the reason for his unease, because they were convinced that the shipowner's sorrow was naturally not his personal matter.

"Ladies and gentlemen!" The shipowner said hesitantly, with a fireless cigarette holder in his fingers. He no longer paid attention to it. "Gentlemen! Our 'Adel' has not broken any parts, nor has it encountered any danger. It can safely take us to our destination. It's just that we lack our drinking water. According to the kitchen report, the fresh water stored on the ship is only enough for two days of use. After two days, we will no longer have fresh water. This has a very large impact on your health. We still have eight days of journey. We will be cut off from fresh water for one hundred and forty-four hours!"

So the crowd on the deck stirred up a great commotion. Disorderly discussions were boiling. Some ran into the kitchen to inspect the water tanks, some were yelling angrily, and some were reporting the news to all the people they knew or didn't know.

"What are we going to do? Mr. William!" A passenger questioned the shipowner impatiently.

"Mr. William! This is your responsibility!" Another shouted.

"Yes, yes." The shipowner nodded pitifully, putting his hands in his trouser pockets, with a helpless expression of calmness on his face, leaning against the railing like a puppet.

"Oh, we're really unlucky to be on this unlucky passenger ship." The gentleman's wife pouted and muttered!

"How can we do without fresh water? Seawater is not good to drink. We are not used to being saltwater fish." The young ladies said shrilly, shaking their heads with unhappy faces.

"How can we do without fresh water?" Everyone echoed in unison.

The shipowner spoke again: "Let me send a telegram to a neighboring ship. Perhaps they can help a little and send us some fresh water, which is still unknown." The telegram was sent, and everyone waited silently for a reply for the time being. Not long after, a reply telegram came, not agreeing to their request, but giving them an effective instruction. The neighboring ship's telegram said: "Your ship is sailing in fresh water. You need fresh water. Please load up as much as possible nearby!"

So the crew scooped up a bucket of water and tasted it, and it was indeed fresh water. So the whole ship was amazed at this wonderful encounter. They rejoiced at finding life in despair, and prayed to thank God, believing that God's gift was abundant and His compassion for people was all-encompassing.

The shipowner, with a mouthful of fresh water, unfolded his smiling dimples. He did not want to thank God for his great kindness. He thought that a ship immersed in fresh water would also ask others for help with fresh water, so he deeply sighed, "People in happiness do not know they are happy!"

The passengers were satisfied, even happier than before they discovered the fresh water.

Page 23

Training and Cultivation

Theory and Practice

— Fu Zhi

I remember that during the Ming Dynasty, there was a man in Jiangnan named Wu Shi. He was originally a fair-faced scholar who was completely ignorant of martial arts and military strategy. He merely read some of the "Yin Fu Conspiracy" of Taigong and the military strategies of Sun Wu on the surface. He boasted about himself in his hometown, saying how well he understood the mysteries of Sun Wu's military strategies and how he could use troops well. He also gathered many peers to his home and followed what the books said to practice the methods of "striking, stabbing, sitting, and acting." He thought he was "unparalleled in the world," but when the Yuan people invaded at the end of the Ming Dynasty, the country heard of his great name and asked him to be a general. He still "followed the book," using the "striking, stabbing, sitting, and acting methods" that he had pondered in his house to deal with the enemy. But when he got to the battlefield, it turned out that it was not the same thing. What he had studied was useless, and as a result, he was captured by the Yuan soldiers.

From this story, we know that simply sitting and talking without actually taking action is certainly "building a car behind closed doors that doesn't fit when you go out." Moreover, even if you act, if your action is confined to a house and is isolated from the actual activities of society, then no matter how hard you act, it is still "building a car behind closed doors that doesn't fit when you go out."

Speaking of Wang Yangming of the Ming Dynasty, I am afraid everyone knows him. He was a master of Neo-Confucianism, specializing in "clarifying the mind and seeing the nature" and "investigating things to extend knowledge." He can be regarded as having achieved something in learning theory. But one day, he wanted to use his "investigating things to extend knowledge" skill to "investigate" the bamboo in front of the court. He "investigated" it for three days, not only did he not understand the bamboo at all, but also his brain was "investigated" and his body became ill. Only then did he give up using his "investigating things to extend knowledge" skill to investigate real objects and instead went to "investigate material desires and extend innate knowledge." What is gratifying is that after suffering this hardship, he actually proposed the theory of "unity of knowledge and action." This theory means that knowledge—that is, theory—and action—that is, practice—are inseparable. He also said, "Knowing is acting, and acting is knowing."

The above is based on the aspect of only talking and not acting, that is, only talking about theory and not practicing. What about those who only practice and do not study theory?

"Old farmers" and "old gardeners" must be considered to be practicing every day in agriculture and horticulture, but why can't they improve and advance agriculture and horticulture? Why have these two remained in primitive management methods for thousands of years? Some patriots are undoubtedly extremely loyal to the nation and the country. They can commit suicide by jumping into the river, organize blood soul assassination groups, and sacrifice their lives to love the country. This must be said to be brave practice and action, but is such narrow patriotism really beneficial to the nation and the country?

From this point of view, "sitting and talking" without "getting up and acting" is certainly wrong, but simply practicing without studying theory is also impossible, especially in today's society.

Originally, human life is a process of practical action. The Chinese Lao Tzu and the German Goethe both said, "In the beginning was the act," which shows that action comes first and practice comes first. But as human society progressed, human practice and human social activities constituted many experiences. Later actions are the continuation of previous experiences. If later actions are not based on previous experiences, wouldn't we still have to "drill wood to make fire" and "drink blood" now? Later actions use the experience gained from the results of previous actions to guide present actions and help present practice. Since this is the case, we should study the results of previous actions before acting. Organizing those experiences becomes theory. Theory originally comes from practice, and later it can guide and help practice. Furthermore, future practice must be guided by the theories of past and present practice results, so past and present practice is refined into a theory for future practice. In short, this means that theory cannot be separated from practice, and practice cannot be separated from theory.

Some people think that theory and practice can be separated, exist independently, and can be divided into different tasks. This is not right. There is absolutely no theory in the world that can develop absolutely independently without practice. All scientific theories will never progress if they are not used in engineering practice. All social theories, if they are irrelevant to the current society and cannot contribute to the improvement or transformation of society, will lose their qualification as social theories. Therefore, for theory to be able to develop, it must not only be a concrete theory, a theory produced from practice, and a theory that conforms to reality, but also during this period and stage of becoming a theory, it must be constantly integrated into and permeate the practice process. Practice is constantly accompanied by theory, using theory as a compass and proceeding in this direction. At the same time, in the process of practice, theory is constantly being verified, revised, and enriched. Engineering practice progresses and science also progresses. Science progresses and engineering practice also progresses. In the course of social movements, social policies and social theories are produced. At the same time, these theories guide social improvement and social transformation. "Theory without practice is empty, and practice without theory is blind." Theory and practice are unified in this process of contradictory development. Some people only grasp the famous saying "Without theory, there is no action," and think that theory can be studied independently and developed independently, which is not right. As for raising theory because of this sentence, thinking that theory is standing on the commanding heights, issuing orders, and directing practice, that is even more wrong. If we say so, then we can go to the battlefield to charge into battle by simply studying Sun Wu's military books in the house. Isn't this as ridiculous as that boastful Wu Shi? If theory is standing high on the commanding heights directing practice, then that kind of theory is also unrealistic and does not conform to reality. How can it still guide practice?

In fact, practice is the most important and fundamental. Blind practice is certainly wrong, but theory always arises from practice and is for the sake of practice. Moreover, the correctness or error of theory must be corrected in practice. Incorrect theories are overthrown and revised in the process of social practice, and practice creates theories that conform to itself. Moreover, whether a theory is correct or not is not determined solely by the comparison of various theories, but by whether that theory conforms to reality. Therefore, in conclusion, theory and practice are both important, but practice is still the leading factor.

Today's society has reached the most contradictory stage, and people can no longer survive blindly in it—regardless of the country and the individual. We should acquire the legacy of theory to engage in practice, and especially learn theory and generate theory in practice.

Introduction to "How to Study Philosophy"

(Written by Wang Teff, published by Sanjiang Bookstore, priced at seven corners)

The author of this book has written many theoretical works on philosophy and science. This book, "How to Study Philosophy," is his recent work. The whole book uses new viewpoints and methods to systematically and comprehensively explain how to study philosophy. The writing is exceptionally fluent and popular, but the content is not superficial.

The content of this book is divided into nine chapters: Chapter 1, "What Kind of Science is Philosophy," includes the objects dealt with by philosophy, the types of philosophy, and what kind of science philosophy is. Chapter 2, "Why Should We Study Philosophy," includes philosophy and life, philosophy and science, etc. Chapter 3 is "The Empirical and Experimental Methods of Studying Philosophy," Chapter 4 is "How to Conduct Analytical Research," Chapter 5 is "How to Conduct Comprehensive Research," Chapter 6 is "How to Conduct Critical Research," Chapter 7 is "The Steps of Research," and Chapters 8 and 9 are on the outline of philosophy, indicating a concrete posture of philosophy for readers.

In this small work, it not only provides us with a method of philosophical research and a philosophical outline, but also reveals many new opinions. It especially elaborates on correct arguments on the issues that are currently being debated most fiercely in the philosophical world, such as the "existence and abolition of philosophy," the "relationship between philosophy and science," and the "internal divisions of philosophy." This is a point that those who study philosophy in general should pay special attention to.

Folklore

Talking about Hakka Customs

— Xin Chu

I came to the South for business and spent nearly a year among the Hakka people in Fujian and Guangdong. During this period, I often came into contact with Hakka people. I think the Hakka people are somewhat different from other ethnic groups in China. Perhaps the Hakka people themselves and foreigners who have lived in the Hakka people for a long time do not know this very well, because they are all used to it.

The Hakka people migrated from the Central Plains. This has been clarified by experts in all aspects; for example, regarding the textual research on the Hakka people's migration from the Central Plains, some people say that they migrated three times, and some people say that they only migrated twice. However, regardless of whether it was two or three times, it is generally recognized that the Hakka people migrated from the Central Plains. In linguistics, Yang Gongheng has proved that the Hakka language has many ancient sounds of the Central Plains; the recent Confucian Yi Taiyan's "Lingwai Erzhou Language" also proves that the essence of the Hakka language is no different from that of the Central Plains. Furthermore, in terms of the Hakka people's genealogy, if you ask any Hakka person, they will tell you: which province their ancestors migrated from; if you ask a slightly educated Hakka person, they will also tell you: in what era, from what place, and why they migrated here. Although the era they migrated from, the earliest group was in the eleventh and twelfth centuries (Song Dynasty), they still retain the name of Hakka people. If they meet Hakka people
